Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
6 min
Definition and Conditions of Idhtirab vs Ikhtilaf
Defining idhtirab and its distinction from ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define idhtirab, state its three conditions, and distinguish it from ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
Idhtirab requires equal conflicting narrations; if one outweighs, it's just ikhtilaf, not a defect.

This passage introduces two key terms in hadith criticism: idhtirab (disorder) and ikhtilaf (disagreement). Understanding the precise conditions of idhtirab is essential for evaluating conflicting narrations and their impact on legal rulings. The text clarifies that not every disagreement constitutes a defect—only when versions are equally strong and irreconcilable does the hadith become mudtarib and thus weakened.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key terms
Locate the terms 'idhtirab' and 'ikhtilaf' in the passage. Note that idhtirab is a specific type of ikhtilaf with stricter conditions.
These are foundational terms in usul al-hadith.
2
State the primary condition of idhtirab
The passage states that idhtirab requires the conflicting narrations to be equal in strength (tasāwī al-riwāyāt). Neither version can outweigh the other.
This is the core distinguishing condition.
3
Apply the condition of tarjīh
If one narration is stronger (e.g., narrator more reliable), it is given preference and the weaker is discarded as shādhdh or munkar. This is not idhtirab.
Tarjīh (preference) nullifies idhtirab.
4
Examine the possibility of jam‘ (reconciliation)
If the conflicting versions can be harmonized (e.g., one names an otherwise ambiguous narrator), there is no idhtirab. The passage gives the example of 'from a man' vs. naming him.
Jam‘ prevents idhtirab even without tarjīh.
5
Understand the general-specific relationship
Every idhtirab is an ikhtilaf, but not every ikhtilaf is idhtirab. Only detrimental ikhtilāf with equal strength and no reconciliation is idhtirab.
The passage states: 'kull muḍṭarib mukhtalaf fīh, wa lā ‘aks'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل التمهيدي بيان ماهية الاختلاف
ومن شرط الاضطراب تساوي الروايات المضطربة بحيث لا تترجح إحداها عَلَى الأخرى.
أما إذا ترجحت إحدى الروايات فلا يسمى مضطرباً، بَلْ هُوَ مطلق اختلافٍ، قَالَ العراقي: «أما إذا ترجحت إحداهما بكون راويها أحفظ أو أكثر صُحْبَة للمروي عَنْهُ، أو غَيْر ذَلِكَ من وجوه الترجيح؛ فإنه لا يطلق على الوجه الراجح وصف الاضطراب ولا له حكمه، والحكم حينئذ للوجه الراجح». وهذا أمر معروف بَيْنَ الْمُحَدِّثِينَ لا خلاف فيه؛ لذا نجد المباركفوري يَقُوْلُ: «قَدْ تقرر في أصول الحَدِيث أن مجرد الاختلاف لا يوجب الاضطراب، بَلْ من شرطه استواء وجوه الاختلاف فمتى رجح أحد الأقوال قدّم». فعلى هَذَا شرط الاضطراب تساوي الروايات، أما إذا ترجحت إحداهما عَلَى الأخرى فالحكم للراجحة، والمرجوحة شاذة أو منكرة. وعليه فإن كان أحد الوجوه مروياً مِنْ طريق ضعيف والآخر من طريق قوي فلا اضطراب والعمل بالطريق القوي، وإِن لَمْ يَكُنْ كذلك، فإن أمكن الجمع بَيْنَ تِلْكَ الوجوه بحيث يمكن أن يَكُونَ المتكلم باللفظين الواردين عن معنى واحد فلا إشكال أَيضاً ؛ مِثْل أَن يَكُوْنَ فِي أحد الوَجْهَيْنِ قَدْ قَالَ الرَّاوِي: عَنْ رَجُلٍ، وفي الوجه الآخر يسمي هَذَا الرجل، فَقَدْ يَكُوْن هَذَا المسمى هُوَ ذَلِكَ المبهم؛ فَلاَ اضطراب إذن ولا تعارض وإن لَمْ يَكُنْ كَذَلِكَ بأن يسمي الرَّاوِي باسم معين في رِوَايَة ويسميه باسم آخر في رِوَايَة أخرى فهذا محل نظر وَهُوَ اضطراب إذ يتعارض فيه أمران:
أحدهما: أنه يجوز أن يَكُون الْحَدِيث عَنْ الرجلين معاً.
والثاني: أن يغلب عَلَى الظن أن الرَّاوِي واحد واختلف فيه). فههنا لا يخلو أن يَكُون الرجلان كلاهما ثقة أو لا، فإن كانا ثقتين فهنا لا يضر الاختلاف عِنْدَ الكثير؛ لأنّ الاختلاف كيف دار فهو عَلَى ثقة وبعضهم يقول: هَذَا اضطراب يضر؛ لأنه يدل عَلَى قلة الضبط. إذن شرط الاضطراب الاتحاد في المصدر، وعدم إمكانية التوفيق بَيْنَ الوجوه المختلفة والترجيح عَلَى منهج النقاد وعلى ما تقدم يتبين لنا أن بَيْنَ الاضطراب والاختلاف عموماً وخصوصاً، وَهُوَ أن كُلّ مضطرب مختلف فيه، ولا عكس. فالاختلاف أعم من الاضطراب إذْ شرط الاضطراب أن يَكُون قادحاً، أما الاختلاف فربما كان قادحاً وربما لَمْ يَكُنْ قادحاً.
ثُمَّ إنه ليس كُلّ اختلاف يؤدي إلى وجود الاضطراب، إذ إن ما يشبه أن يَكُوْن اضطراباً ينتفي عَنْ الْحَدِيْث إذا جمع بَيْنَ الوجوه المختلفة أو رجح وجه مِنْهَا عَلَى طريقة النقاد لا على طريقة التجويز العقلي.
Preliminary chapter: Explanation of the nature of disagreement. Among the conditions of idhtirab is the equipollence of conflicting narrations such that none outweighs the other. If one narration is outweighed, it is not called idhtirab, but rather it is absolute disagreement. Al-Iraqi said: 'If one of them is outweighed due to its narrator being more retentive or having more companionship with the one narrated from, or other aspects of preference, then the preferred version is not described as idhtirab nor does it have its ruling; the ruling then is for the preferred version.' This is well-known among hadith scholars without dispute; hence al-Mubarakfuri says: 'It has been established in hadith principles that mere disagreement does not cause idhtirab, but rather its condition is the equal weight of the aspects of disagreement; when one opinion is preferred, it is given priority.' So the condition of idhtirab is the equality of narrations; if one outweighs the other, the ruling is for the preponderant, and the outweighed is irregular or rejected. Accordingly, if one version is narrated through a weak chain and another through a strong chain, there is no idhtirab and the strong chain is acted upon. If not, and reconciliation between those versions is possible such that the speaker may have intended the same meaning by the two wordings, then there is no issue either. For example, if in one version the narrator said 'from a man' and in the other he names that man, then this named person may be the same as the ambiguous one; so there is no idhtirab and no contradiction. But if not, such as the narrator naming a specific person in one narration and another name in another, this is a point of consideration and it is idhtirab because two matters conflict: first, it is possible that the hadith is from both men; second, it is likely that the narrator is one and differed about him. So here it cannot be avoided that the two men are both reliable or not. If both are reliable, then disagreement does not harm according to many, because whichever way it goes, it is based on a reliable person; but some say this is harmful idhtirab because it indicates lack of precision. So the condition of idhtirab is unity of source, impossibility of reconciliation between the different versions, and preference according to the method of critics. From what precedes, we see that idhtirab and ikhtilaf have a general-specific relationship: every idhtirab is involved in ikhtilaf, but not vice versa. Thus ikhtilaf is more general than idhtirab, since the condition of idhtirab is that it is detrimental, while ikhtilaf may or may not be detrimental. Moreover, not every ikhtilaf leads to idhtirab, because what appears to be idhtirab is negated from the hadith if the different versions are reconciled or one version is preferred according to the method of critics, not according to intellectual possibility.
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage is a definition and delineation of two key terms in hadith criticism: idhtirab (disorder/confusion) and ikhtilaf (disagreement). The author clarifies that the core condition for a hadith to be considered mudtarib is that the conflicting narrations are equal in strength — neither can be given preponderance over the other. If one version is clearly stronger (e.g., due to a more reliable narrator or greater companionship with the source), then the weaker version is discarded as irregular, and we are dealing with mere ikhtilaf, not idhtirab. The author supports this with quotes from al-Iraqi and al-Mubarakfuri, showing consensus among hadith scholars. Then the text explores scenarios: when one version is weak and the other strong, there is no idhtirab; when reconciliation is possible (like naming an ambiguous narrator), there is no problem; but when the narrator contradicts himself by naming different people, it becomes problematic. The passage also examines the case where both narrators are reliable: some scholars say this does not cause idhtirab because the discrepancy still rests on reliable sources, while others consider it harmful because it shows lack of memorization. Finally, the relationship between the two concepts is clarified: every mudtarib hadith is an instance of ikhtilaf, but not every ikhtilaf constitutes idhtirab. This is a fundamental distinction in usul al-hadith that affects how jurists evaluate conflicting reports.

Key Terms
الاضطراب (al-idtirab): تساوي الروايات المتعارضة بحيث لا تترجح إحداها على الأخرى مع اتحاد المصدر وعدم إمكان التوفيق أو الترجيح
الاختلاف (al-ikhtilaf): مطلق عدم التوافق بين الروايات، سواء كان مع الترجيح أو بدونه، وقد يكون قادحاً وقد لا يكون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
ما شرط الاضطراب في الحديث عند المحدثين؟
A) وجود اختلاف بين الروايات مطلقاً
B) تساوي الروايات المتعارضة بحيث لا تترجح إحداها على الأخرى مع استحالة التوفيق
C) كون الروايات كلها ضعيفة
D) اختلاف الرواة في الإسناد فقط

Key Takeaway
Idhtirab requires equal, irreconcilable versions; ikhtilaf is broader and may be harmless.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement

The Nature of Disagreement Among Narrators and Detecting Idtirab
Introducing the causes of variation in hadith transmission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the causes of variation in hadith transmission and apply the methodological rule that idtirab is recognized only through collecting all chains.

Core Idea
Idtirab in hadith cannot be inferred from a single text; it requires systematic collection of all available chains.

This passage lays the methodological foundation for understanding why narrators differ in their transmission of hadiths. It emphasizes that such variation is natural due to differences in memory, precision, circumstances, and care. The key technical term introduced is 'idtirab' – a type of disagreement that cannot be resolved by preference or reconciliation. Crucially, the author insists that idtirab is not apparent from a single narration but only emerges when all chains of a hadith are collected and studied systematically. This rule is essential for any student of usul al-fiqh who wishes to evaluate the reliability of hadiths that may appear contradictory.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the Source of Variation
Identify the author's claim that variation among narrators is natural. Note the factors mentioned: differences in innate memorization ability, fluctuations in precision due to age and health, and varying levels of care in preserving hadiths.
This step grounds you in the reality of human imperfection in transmission.
2
List the Factors Affecting Dabt
Extract from the text the specific factors that affect a narrator's precision (dabt): differing talents, changing circumstances, health, and the habit of reviewing and consulting sources. Some narrators only narrate with a clear mind and after checking their written records.
Dabt is a key condition for accepting a narrator's hadiths.
3
Define Idtirab
From the passage, understand that idtirab is a type of disagreement among the various transmissions of a hadith such that no single version can be preferred over others and they cannot be harmonized. It is a critical defect in the hadith.
The author stresses that idtirab is not a flaw in a single chain but a relationship among multiple chains.
4
Apply the Detection Method
The text explicitly states that idtirab is not known from the apparent context of a single hadith. It is only recognized by collecting all the chains of a hadith and studying them methodically, combining understanding, knowledge, and practical experience in hadith criticism.
This rule guards against hasty judgments based on limited data.

Source Text

المبحث الثالث
أنواع الاختلاف
من البدهي أن يختلف الرُّوَاة سنداً ومتناً فيما يؤدونه من الأحاديث النبوية؛ ذَلِكَ لأن مواهب الرُّوَاة في حفظ الأحاديث تختلف اختلافاً جذرياً بَيْنَ راو وآخر، فمن الرُّوَاة من بلغ أعلى مراتب الحفظ والضبط والإتقان ومنهم أدنى وأدنى. ولا عجب يختل ضبط الرُّوَاة من حال إلى حال ومن وقت إلى وقت مع تغيرات الزمان واختلاف الأحوال وتبدل الصحة هَذَا مع اختلاف الرُّوَاة في عنايتهم في ضبط ما يتحملونه من الأحاديث فمنهم من يتعاهد حفظه ومنهم من لا يتعاهد، ومنهم من لا يحدث إلا بصفاء الذهن ومراجعة الأصول ومنهم دون ذَلِكَ. زيادة عَلَى الآفات الَّتِي تصيب حفظه، ثُمَّ إنّ الاضطراب لا يعرف من ظاهر سياق الحَدِيث الواحد، بل يعرف الاضطراب بجمع طرق الحَدِيث و دراستها دراسة منهجية مع الفهم والمعرفة والممارسة الحديثية.
Third section: Types of disagreement. It is obvious that narrators differ in chain and text in the prophetic hadiths they transmit, because the abilities of narrators in memorizing hadiths differ radically between one narrator and another. Among narrators are those who reached the highest levels of memorization, precision, and mastery, and among them are lower and lower. And there is no wonder that the precision of narrators varies from one state to another and from time to time with changes of time, differing circumstances, and alteration of health. This is in addition to the narrators' differing care in preserving what they receive of hadiths: some regularly review their memorization, some do not, some only narrate with a clear mind and review of sources, and others are below that. Additionally, there are the defects that affect their memorization. Furthermore, idhtirab is not known from the apparent context of a single hadith, but rather idhtirab is known by collecting the chains of a hadith and studying them methodically with understanding, knowledge, and hadith practice.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage is the opening of a new section on the types of disagreement among narrators. The author states a basic premise: it is natural that narrators differ in both the chain (sanad) and text (matn) of the hadiths they transmit. The reason lies in the innate differences in memorization abilities among narrators; some are at the pinnacle of precision and mastery, while others are far below. Moreover, the same narrator's precision can fluctuate due to age, circumstances, and health. Another factor is the level of care they take in preserving what they have learned: some constantly review their memorization, some do not, and some will only narrate when their mind is clear and they have consulted their written sources. Additionally, there are external defects that can affect their memorization. Finally, the author reiterates a crucial point: idhtirab cannot be detected by looking at a single hadith text; it is only recognized by collecting all the chains of a hadith and studying them systematically with proper understanding, knowledge, and practical experience in hadith criticism. This serves as a methodological foundation for the detailed discussion of types of disagreement that follows.

Key Terms
الضبط (al-dabt): إتقان الحديث وحفظه بحيث يمكن استحضاره عند الرواية بدون تغيير
الاضطراب (al-idtirab): اختلاف الروايات بحيث لا يمكن الترجيح ولا الجمع، ولا يعرف إلا بجمع الطرق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
كيف يُعرف الاضطراب في الحديث وفقاً لهذا النص؟
A) بظاهر سياق الحديث الواحد
B) بجمع طرق الحديث ودراستها منهجياً
C) بكثرة رواة الحديث
D) بضعف بعض الرواة

Key Takeaway
Idtirab is a collective judgment requiring comprehensive study of all narrations, not a single-text evaluation.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
beginner

The Difference Between Mudtarib and Ikhtilaf
Defines mudtarib and distinguishes it from general ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish mudtarib from ikhtilaf and identify the conditions that make a hadith mudtarib according to Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Mudtarib is a harmful subset of ikhtilaf; not every difference among trustworthy narrators makes a hadith defective.

In hadith criticism, scholars often encounter conflicting narrations. Not every conflict weakens a hadith. This passage clarifies the precise condition that elevates a difference into a defect (mudtarib), distinguishing it from harmless ikhtilaf. Understanding this distinction is essential for Hanafi usul, as it affects the weight of evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Notice the passage considers whether narrators are trustworthy or not. If both are trustworthy, the difference is generally not harmful; otherwise, it may be problematic.
2
Understand the opposing view
Some scholars argue that even conflict among trustworthy narrators indicates lack of precision and thus constitutes mudtarib. Recognize that this is a stricter position.
The Hanafi school tends to prefer reconciliation first, but acknowledges this view.
3
Extract the conditions for mudtarib
The passage states: unity of source (same narrator) and impossibility of reconciliation or tarjih (preference) by critical methods (not mere mental possibility). These are the two key conditions.
Tarjih must follow established critical methods, not arbitrary preference.
4
Apply the general-specific relationship
Every mudtarib hadith involves ikhtilaf, but not every ikhtilaf is mudtarib. Ikhtilaf is broader; it may be harmless if reconciliation or tarjih is possible.
This logical relationship is crucial for evaluating hadith strength.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يَكُون الرجلان كلاهما ثقة أو لا، فإن كانا ثقتين فهنا لا يضر الاختلاف عِنْدَ الكثير؛ لأنّ الاختلاف كيف دار فهو عَلَى ثقة وبعضهم يقول: هَذَا اضطراب يضر؛ لأنه يدل عَلَى قلة الضبط. إذن شرط الاضطراب الاتحاد في المصدر، وعدم إمكانية التوفيق بَيْنَ الوجوه المختلفة والترجيح عَلَى منهج النقاد وعلى ما تقدم يتبين لنا أن بَيْنَ الاضطراب والاختلاف عموماً وخصوصاً، وَهُوَ أن كُلّ مضطرب مختلف فيه، ولا عكس. فالاختلاف أعم من الاضطراب إذْ شرط الاضطراب أن يَكُون قادحاً، أما الاختلاف فربما كان قادحاً وربما لَمْ يَكُنْ قادحاً. ثُمَّ إنه ليس كُلّ اختلاف يؤدي إلى وجود الاضطراب، إذ إن ما يشبه أن يَكُوْن اضطراباً ينتفي عَنْ الْحَدِيْث إذا جمع بَيْنَ الوجوه المختلفة أو رجح وجه مِنْهَا عَلَى طريقة النقاد لا على طريقة التجويز العقلي.
The two men may both be trustworthy or not. If both are trustworthy, then the difference does not harm according to many, because wherever the difference occurs it is upon a trustworthy narrator. Some say this is a disorder that harms because it indicates lack of precision. So the condition of disorder is unity of source and the impossibility of reconciliation between the different aspects and of weighing according to the method of critics. Based on the above, it becomes clear to us that between disorder and difference there is a general-specific relation: every disordered hadith is subject to difference, but not vice versa. Thus difference is more general than disorder, since the condition of disorder is that it be a defect, while difference may be defective or not. Furthermore, not every difference leads to the existence of disorder, for what appears to be disorder is removed from the hadith if the different aspects are combined or one aspect is favored according to the method of critics, not by mere mental possibility.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage defines the concept of mudtarib (disordered hadith) in relation to ikhtilaf (difference). The author notes that if two narrators are both trustworthy, their difference is typically not harmful, as both are reliable. However, some scholars consider such a difference as mudtarib if it indicates poor memory or lack of precision. The key condition for mudtarib is that the conflicting narrations come from the same source and cannot be reconciled or preferred one over the other by established critical methods. Mudtarib is thus a subset of ikhtilaf — every mudtarib involves ikhtilaf, but not every ikhtilaf rises to the level of mudtarib. The harmfulness of mudtarib disqualifies the hadith, whereas general ikhtilaf may be resolved through reconciliation or tarjih. This is an important distinction in hadith criticism, as it helps scholars assess the strength of conflicting narrations.

Key Terms
الاضطراب (al-mudtarib): A hadith condition where conflicting narrations from the same source cannot be reconciled or weighed; a defect.
الاختلاف (al-ikhtilaf): General difference or disagreement among narrators, which may be harmless or defective.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the condition for a hadith to be considered mudtarib (disordered)?
A) The narrators are both trustworthy.
B) The difference arises from different sources.
C) The conflicting narrations come from the same source and cannot be reconciled or favored.
D) The difference is in the wording only.

Key Takeaway
Mudtarib is a specific defect requiring unity of source and irreconcilability, while ikhtilaf is a broader concept that includes harmless differences.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
beginner

Two Types of Ikhtilaf: Tanawwu' and Tadadd
Classification of hadith differences into harmless variety and harmful contradiction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between ikhtilaf al-tanawwu' and ikhtilaf al-tadadd and identify which type harms a hadith's authenticity according to Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Not all differences among narrators harm a hadith; only unresolved contradictions (tadadd) are defects.

In hadith criticism, narrators often differ in how they report a hadith. Some differences are superficial, while others indicate real conflict. This lesson introduces two categories that help us assess whether a difference affects the hadith's reliability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main types
Recognize that narrators' differences are classified into ikhtilaf al-tanawwu' (variety) and ikhtilaf al-tadadd (contradiction).
Tanawwu' is harmless; tadadd is harmful.
2
Understand ikhtilaf al-tanawwu'
This type involves variation in expression (e.g., name vs. kunyah, different wording) while the underlying meaning remains the same. It does not affect authenticity.
Example: calling a narrator by his name vs. his nickname.
3
Understand ikhtilaf al-tadadd
This is genuine contradiction where two narrations cannot be reconciled or one cannot be preferred over the other. It is a defect that weakens the hadith.
Requires impossibility of tawfiq (reconciliation) or tarjih (weighing).
4
Apply the classification
Given a specific case of narrator difference, determine whether it falls under tanawwu' or tadadd and explain the impact on the hadith's authenticity.
Use the criteria: can the difference be resolved without contradicting the meaning?

المبحث الثالث
أنواع الاختلاف
من البدهي أن يختلف الرُّوَاة سنداً ومتناً فيما يؤدونه من الأحاديث النبوية؛ ذَلِكَ
لأن مواهب الرُّوَاة في حفظ الأحاديث تختلف اختلافاً جذرياً بَيْنَ راو وآخر، فمن
الرُّوَاة من بلغ أعلى مراتب الحفظ والضبط والإتقان ومنهم أدنى وأدنى. ولا عجب أن
yختل ضبط الرُّوَاة من حال إلى حال ومن وقت إلى وقت مع تغيرات الزمان واختلاف الأحوال وتبدل الصحة هَذَا مع اختلاف الرُّوَاة في عنايتهم في ضبط ما يتحملونه من الأحاديث فمنهم من يتعاهد حفظه ومنهم من لا يتعاهد، ومنهم من لا يحدث إلا بصفاء الذهن ومراجعة الأصول ومنهم دون ذَلِكَ. زيادة عَلَى الآفات الَّتِي تصيب الإنسان مِمَّا تؤدي إلى اختلال مروياته ودخول بعض الوهم في حديثه. فهذا كله من الأسباب الرئيسة العامة في وجود الاختلاف.
أم إن اختلاف الرُّوَاة يرجع إلى نوعين رئيسين: اختلاف تنوع، واختلاف تضاد.
فاختلاف التنوع: هُوَ أن يذكر كُلّ من المختلفين من الاسم أو اللفظ بعض أنواعه، كأن يختلف الرُّوَاة عَلَى راو فبعضهم يذكره باسمه وبعضهم يذكره بكنيته وبعضهم بلقبه وبعضهم بوصف اشتهر به وربما أطلق عَلَى هَذَا الاختلاف اختلاف في العبارة وَهُوَ : أن يعبر كُلّ من المختلفين عَنْ المراد بعبارة غير عبارة صاحبه، والمعنى واحد عِنْدَ الْجَمِيع.
والنوع الآخر من أنواع الاختلاف اختلاف التضاد وَهُوَ الاختلاف الحقيقي القادح، وَهُوَ : أن يختلفِ الرُّوَاة في متن حديثين أحدهما يخالف أو ينافي الآخر أو أن يختلف الرُّوَاة في راوِ أو رواة مختلفين عن الآخرين مع عدم إمكان الترجيح والتوفيق على طريقة النقاد؛ إذ تتساوى وجوه الروايات.
Third Section: Types of Difference. It is evident that narrators differ in chain and text in what they transmit of Prophetic hadiths. That is because the abilities of narrators in memorizing hadiths differ radically between one narrator and another. Some narrators reach the highest levels of memorization, precision, and mastery, while others are lower and lower. And it is no wonder that the precision of narrators varies from situation to situation and from time to time with changes in time and differing conditions and changes in health. All this is in addition to the afflictions that affect a person leading to the corruption of his narrations and the entry of some illusion in his hadith. This is all among the main general causes for the existence of difference. But the difference of narrators goes back to two main types: difference of variety, and difference of contradiction. Difference of variety: that each of those differing mentions some types of the name or word, such as the narrators differing over a narrator, some mentioning him by his name, some by his patronymic, some by his nickname, some by a description he is famous for. Sometimes this difference is called difference in expression: that each of those differing expresses the intended meaning with a different expression from his companion, yet the meaning is the same according to all. The other type is difference of contradiction, which is the real defective difference: that the narrators differ in the text of two hadiths, one contradicting or conflicting with the other, or that the narrators differ over a narrator or different narrators from others with no possibility of weighing or reconciliation according to the method of critics, as the aspects of narrations are equal.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage categorizes the differences found among hadith narrators into two main types. The first, ikhtilaf al-tanawwu' (difference of variety), refers to differences that are not substantive, such as referring to the same person by his name, kunyah, or laqab, or expressing the same meaning in different words. These differences do not harm the authenticity of the hadith because they can be reconciled. The second, ikhtilaf al-tadadd (difference of contradiction), is a genuine conflict where two narrations directly oppose each other or cannot be reconciled or one cannot be preferred over the other through critical methods. This type is considered a defect in the hadith. The author emphasizes that the possibility of reconciliation or tarjih is determined by the established methodology of hadith critics, not by mere personal judgment.

Key Terms
اختلاف التنوع (ikhtilaf al-tanawwu'): Difference of variety: harmless variation in naming or expression while the underlying meaning is the same.
اختلاف التضاد (ikhtilaf al-tadadd): Difference of contradiction: genuine conflict in content or chain that cannot be resolved, harmful to hadith authenticity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What distinguishes ikhtilaf al-tadadd from ikhtilaf al-tanawwu'?
A) Tadadd occurs only in the chain; tanawwu' only in the text.
B) Tadadd is a genuine contradiction that cannot be resolved, while tanawwu' is a superficial variation that can be reconciled.
C) Tadadd always involves weak narrators; tanawwu' involves strong narrators.
D) Both are harmful, but tadadd is more severe.

Key Takeaway
Hanafi usul classifies narrator differences into harmless variety (tanawwu') and harmful contradiction (tadadd), with only the latter affecting hadith authenticity.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
beginner
8 min
Types of Narrator Differences: Variety vs Contradiction
Defines two types of ikhtilaf among narrators.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between ikhtilāf al-tanawwuʿ and ikhtilāf al-taḍādd, and state which type is damaging to hadith authenticity.

Core Idea
Ikhtilāf al-tanawwuʿ preserves meaning; ikhtilāf al-taḍādd signals real conflict.

In this passage, we learn that not all differences among narrators are equal. Some are merely variations in expression—differences of variety—which do not undermine the underlying unity of meaning. Others are contradictions that cannot be reconciled, pointing to a genuine flaw. Understanding this classification is crucial for the hadith critic and the jurist who relies on sound traditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main types
The passage states that differences among narrators fall into two categories: difference of variety (ikhtilāf al-tanawwuʿ) and difference of contradiction (ikhtilāf al-taḍādd). Note the Arabic terms.
2
Understand 'difference of variety'
This occurs when narrators use different words, names, or descriptions for the same thing; the meaning is identical. For example, referring to a narrator by name vs. kunyah.
Also called 'difference in expression'.
3
Understand 'difference of contradiction'
This is a real conflict where two hadith texts are mutually exclusive, or narrations are irreconcilable and equally strong, with no possibility of preference.
This is damaging to authenticity.
4
Apply the distinction
Given a scenario, classify the type of difference. For instance, if two narrators report the same event with different but synonymous phrases, it is variety; if one says 'the Prophet did X' and another says 'he did not do X', it is contradiction.

بزيادة أو نقص أو تغيير -. بوس ومع هَذَا كله فإننا لم نعدم في تاريخنا الحديثي بعض الرُّوَاةِ الَّذِينَ لَمْ يبالوا بمروياتهم، وَلَمْ يولوها الاهتمام الكافي، سواء أهمل الرَّاوِي نفسه تعاهد محفوظاته أَوْ مراجعته کتابه، أو تدخل عنصر بالعبث بمروياته (۳)، أو غَيْر ذَلِكَ مِمَّا تكون نتيجته وقوع الوهم في حَدِيث ذَلِكَ الرَّاوِي، ويؤول بالنهاية إلى حدوث الاختلاف مع روايات غيره، عَلَى أن الخطأ والوهم لَمْ يسلم مِنْهُ كبار الحفاظ شدة حرصهم وتوقيهم، لذا قَالَ مع (۳): لست أعجب ممن يحدّث فيخطئ، إنما أعجب ممن يحدث فيصيب). غَيْر أنّ الأحاديث الَّتِي حصل فيها الوهم تعد قليلة مغمورة في بحـر مـا رووه عَلَى الصواب. وبإمكاننا أن نفصل أسباب الاختلاف بما يأتي: أولاً. الوهم والخطأ: الخطأ والوهم أمران حاصلان وواقعان في أحاديث الثقات فضلاً عن وقوعه في أحاديث الضعفاء، ونحن وإن نذكر في حد الصَّحِيح كون راويه تام الضبط إلا أن ذَلِكَ أمر نسبي ) ، وإلا فكيف اشترطنا في الصَّحِيح () أن لا يَكُون شاذاً ولا معللاً مع كون راويه ثقة فيتخرج عَلَى هَذَا أن الوهم والخطأ يدخل في أحاديث الثقات؛ لأن كلاً من
The introductory chapter: Explanation of the nature of difference. The human being from what leads to disturbance of his narrations and entry of some delusion into his hadith. So all of this is among the general main causes for the existence of difference. Contradiction (1). Or rather, the difference of narrators goes back to two main types: difference of variety, and difference of contradiction. So difference of variety: it is that each of the different parties mentions from the name or wording some of its types, such as the narrators differing about a narrator: some mention him by his name, some by his kunyah, some by his nickname, and some by a description he is famous for. And perhaps this difference is called difference in expression, and it is that each of the different parties expresses the intended meaning with an expression other than his companion's expression, while the meaning is the same according to all (?). The other type of difference is difference of contradiction, and it is the real, damaging difference. It is that the narrators differ regarding the text of two hadiths, one contradicting or opposing the other, or that the narrators differ regarding one narrator or different narrators from others while it is impossible to give preference or reconcile according to the method of the critics, as the aspects of the narrations are equal. The fourth topic: Causes of difference. Allah the Exalted naturally created people to differ in their talents and abilities and the diversity of their capacities in precision, accuracy, mastery, and care for something. Just as people differ in their other conditions, Allah the Exalted said: 'Then of them are wrongdoers to themselves, and of them are moderate, and of them are foremost in good deeds.' These talents and gifts are from Allah, He gives to whom He wills what He wills. Likewise, people differ in their care and effort. For that reason, Imam al-Shafi'i (4) counted care as a prerequisite of knowledge and said: 'O brother, you will not attain knowledge except through six: I will inform you of its details with a statement: intelligence, care, effort, provision, companionship of a teacher, and length of time.' (1) So care is thus among the basics of knowledge. Even if the narrator's memory is weak or his memory fails, his capacity to preserve his narrations through review, follow-up, constant revision of what he memorizes, and review of his sources, preserves the Prophetic Sunnah from error in it - by addition, omission, or alteration. Bus. And despite all this, we have not lacked in our hadith history some narrators who did not care about their narrations and did not give them sufficient attention, whether the narrator himself neglected constant revision of his memorization or review of his book, or an element of tampering with his narrations (3) interfered, or other things the result of which is the occurrence of delusion in the hadith of that narrator, ultimately leading to the occurrence of difference with the narrations of others. However, error and delusion did not spare even the major preservers despite their intense care and caution. Hence, Ma'n (3) said: 'I do not wonder at the one who narrates and makes mistakes; I only wonder at the one who narrates and is correct.' Yet the hadiths in which delusion occurred are few, submerged in a sea of what they narrated correctly. And we can detail the causes of difference as follows: Firstly: Delusion and error: Error and delusion are two matters that occur and take place in the hadiths of reliable narrators, let alone their occurrence in the hadiths of weak narrators. And although we mention in the definition of the authentic (hadith) that its narrator is complete in precision, that is a relative matter. Otherwise, how could we have stipulated in the authentic (hadith) that it be neither anomalous nor defective while its narrator is trustworthy? From this it follows that delusion and error enter into the hadiths of reliable narrators, because both of
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This passage is an introductory chapter defining the nature and causes of differences among hadith narrators. The author first states that human fallibility is a primary cause of discrepancy in narrations. He then identifies two principal types of difference: (1) Difference of variety (ikhtilāf al-tanawwuʿ), where narrators express the same meaning using different phrases, names, nicknames, or descriptions — this does not constitute a genuine contradiction. (2) Difference of contradiction (ikhtilāf al-taḍādd), a real, damaging discrepancy where two hadith texts are mutually exclusive or where conflicting reports are equally balanced with no possibility of preference or reconciliation. The author then shifts to causes of difference, citing Quranic verse (Fatir:32) to show that people naturally vary in talents and diligence. He quotes Imam al-Shafiʿi's couplet listing six prerequisites for knowledge, emphasizing that care (al-ḥirṣ) is foundational. Even when a narrator's memory is weak, diligent review and preservation can safeguard against error. Despite this, some narrators neglect their material, leading to delusion and contradiction. Importantly, even the most careful narrators are not immune to error, as quoted from Maʿn ibn ʿĪsā. The reported instances of delusion, however, are rare compared to the vast corpus of sound narrations. The passage concludes by beginning a detailed list of causes, starting with 'delusion and error' (al-wahm wa al-khaṭaʾ), asserting that even reliable narrators can fall into these, which is why the definition of an authentic hadith includes the absence of shudhūdh (anomaly) and ʿillah (defect) despite the narrator being trustworthy. This analysis is foundational for understanding how hadith differences impact juristic rulings.

Key Terms
اختلاف التنوع (ikhtilāf al-tanawwuʿ): Difference of variety: narrators express the same meaning using different expressions or descriptions, without contradiction.
اختلاف التضاد (ikhtilāf al-taḍādd): Difference of contradiction: narrations that are mutually exclusive or cannot be reconciled, indicating a genuine conflict.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following best describes ikhtilāf al-taḍādd?
A) Narrators use different synonyms for the same action.
B) Narrators disagree on a non-essential detail but meaning is same.
C) Narrations are mutually exclusive and cannot be reconciled.
D) Narrators differ in chain but text is identical.

Key Takeaway
Not all narrator differences are equal; variety is harmless, contradiction is damaging.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement

Causes of Narrator Differences: Error, Delusion, and Human Fallibility
Discusses causes of difference, especially error and delusion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the primary causes of hadith differences, especially error and delusion, and explain why even reliable narrators can make mistakes.

Core Idea
Human fallibility is the root cause of differences, affecting even the most trustworthy narrators.

This passage explores why narrators differ, tracing it back to the natural variation in human abilities and the inevitable occurrence of error and delusion. It reminds us that even great memorizers are not infallible, though their mistakes are rare. This understanding is essential for a balanced approach to hadith criticism.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the universal nature of human difference
The passage quotes Quran (Fatir:32) to show that people vary in talents, diligence, and concern for accuracy. This is a natural cause of differences.
2
Understand the role of care and effort
Imam al-Shafi'i listed care (al-ḥirṣ) as a prerequisite of knowledge. Care mitigates error, but even the most careful are not immune.
Al-Shafi'i's couplet is cited.
3
Identify the main cause: error and delusion (al-wahm wa al-khaṭaʾ)
The passage states that error and delusion occur even in the hadiths of reliable narrators (thiqāt). This is why the definition of authentic hadith includes absence of shudhūdh and ʿillah despite trustworthy narrator.
4
Note that errors are rare in reliable narrators
The passage assures that the instances of delusion are few compared to the vast sea of correct narrations.

بزيادة أو نقص أو تغيير -. بوس ومع هَذَا كله فإننا لم نعدم في تاريخنا الحديثي بعض الرُّوَاةِ الَّذِينَ لَمْ يبالوا بمروياتهم، وَلَمْ يولوها الاهتمام الكافي، سواء أهمل الرَّاوِي نفسه تعاهد محفوظاته أَوْ مراجعته کتابه، أو تدخل عنصر بالعبث بمروياته (۳)، أو غَيْر ذَلِكَ مِمَّا تكون نتيجته وقوع الوهم في حَدِيث ذَلِكَ الرَّاوِي، ويؤول بالنهاية إلى حدوث الاختلاف مع روايات غيره، عَلَى أن الخطأ والوهم لَمْ يسلم مِنْهُ كبار الحفاظ شدة حرصهم وتوقيهم، لذا قَالَ مع (۳): لست أعجب ممن يحدّث فيخطئ، إنما أعجب ممن يحدث فيصيب). غَيْر أنّ الأحاديث الَّتِي حصل فيها الوهم تعد قليلة مغمورة في بحـر مـا رووه عَلَى الصواب. وبإمكاننا أن نفصل أسباب الاختلاف بما يأتي: أولاً. الوهم والخطأ: الخطأ والوهم أمران حاصلان وواقعان في أحاديث الثقات فضلاً عن وقوعه في أحاديث الضعفاء، ونحن وإن نذكر في حد الصَّحِيح كون راويه تام الضبط إلا أن ذَلِكَ أمر نسبي ) ، وإلا فكيف اشترطنا في الصَّحِيح () أن لا يَكُون شاذاً ولا معللاً مع كون راويه ثقة فيتخرج عَلَى هَذَا أن الوهم والخطأ يدخل في أحاديث الثقات؛ لأن كلاً من
The introductory chapter: Explanation of the nature of difference. The human being from what leads to disturbance of his narrations and entry of some delusion into his hadith. So all of this is among the general main causes for the existence of difference. Contradiction (1). Or rather, the difference of narrators goes back to two main types: difference of variety, and difference of contradiction. So difference of variety: it is that each of the different parties mentions from the name or wording some of its types, such as the narrators differing about a narrator: some mention him by his name, some by his kunyah, some by his nickname, and some by a description he is famous for. And perhaps this difference is called difference in expression, and it is that each of the different parties expresses the intended meaning with an expression other than his companion's expression, while the meaning is the same according to all (?). The other type of difference is difference of contradiction, and it is the real, damaging difference. It is that the narrators differ regarding the text of two hadiths, one contradicting or opposing the other, or that the narrators differ regarding one narrator or different narrators from others while it is impossible to give preference or reconcile according to the method of the critics, as the aspects of the narrations are equal. The fourth topic: Causes of difference. Allah the Exalted naturally created people to differ in their talents and abilities and the diversity of their capacities in precision, accuracy, mastery, and care for something. Just as people differ in their other conditions, Allah the Exalted said: 'Then of them are wrongdoers to themselves, and of them are moderate, and of them are foremost in good deeds.' These talents and gifts are from Allah, He gives to whom He wills what He wills. Likewise, people differ in their care and effort. For that reason, Imam al-Shafi'i (4) counted care as a prerequisite of knowledge and said: 'O brother, you will not attain knowledge except through six: I will inform you of its details with a statement: intelligence, care, effort, provision, companionship of a teacher, and length of time.' (1) So care is thus among the basics of knowledge. Even if the narrator's memory is weak or his memory fails, his capacity to preserve his narrations through review, follow-up, constant revision of what he memorizes, and review of his sources, preserves the Prophetic Sunnah from error in it - by addition, omission, or alteration. Bus. And despite all this, we have not lacked in our hadith history some narrators who did not care about their narrations and did not give them sufficient attention, whether the narrator himself neglected constant revision of his memorization or review of his book, or an element of tampering with his narrations (3) interfered, or other things the result of which is the occurrence of delusion in the hadith of that narrator, ultimately leading to the occurrence of difference with the narrations of others. However, error and delusion did not spare even the major preservers despite their intense care and caution. Hence, Ma'n (3) said: 'I do not wonder at the one who narrates and makes mistakes; I only wonder at the one who narrates and is correct.' Yet the hadiths in which delusion occurred are few, submerged in a sea of what they narrated correctly. And we can detail the causes of difference as follows: Firstly: Delusion and error: Error and delusion are two matters that occur and take place in the hadiths of reliable narrators, let alone their occurrence in the hadiths of weak narrators. And although we mention in the definition of the authentic (hadith) that its narrator is complete in precision, that is a relative matter. Otherwise, how could we have stipulated in the authentic (hadith) that it be neither anomalous nor defective while its narrator is trustworthy? From this it follows that delusion and error enter into the hadiths of reliable narrators, because both of
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This passage is an introductory chapter defining the nature and causes of differences among hadith narrators. The author first states that human fallibility is a primary cause of discrepancy in narrations. He then identifies two principal types of difference: (1) Difference of variety (ikhtilāf al-tanawwuʿ), where narrators express the same meaning using different phrases, names, nicknames, or descriptions — this does not constitute a genuine contradiction. (2) Difference of contradiction (ikhtilāf al-taḍādd), a real, damaging discrepancy where two hadith texts are mutually exclusive or where conflicting reports are equally balanced with no possibility of preference or reconciliation. The author then shifts to causes of difference, citing Quranic verse (Fatir:32) to show that people naturally vary in talents and diligence. He quotes Imam al-Shafiʿi's couplet listing six prerequisites for knowledge, emphasizing that care (al-ḥirṣ) is foundational. Even when a narrator's memory is weak, diligent review and preservation can safeguard against error. Despite this, some narrators neglect their material, leading to delusion and contradiction. Importantly, even the most careful narrators are not immune to error, as quoted from Maʿn ibn ʿĪsā. The reported instances of delusion, however, are rare compared to the vast corpus of sound narrations. The passage concludes by beginning a detailed list of causes, starting with 'delusion and error' (al-wahm wa al-khaṭaʾ), asserting that even reliable narrators can fall into these, which is why the definition of an authentic hadith includes the absence of shudhūdh (anomaly) and ʿillah (defect) despite the narrator being trustworthy. This analysis is foundational for understanding how hadith differences impact juristic rulings.

Key Terms
الوهم والخطأ (al-wahm wa al-khaṭaʾ): Delusion and error: mistakes that can occur even in reliable narrators, leading to differences.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does the definition of an authentic hadith include the condition that it be free from shudhūdh and ʿillah even if the narrator is thiqah?
A) Because thiqah narrators are never mistaken.
B) Because reliable narrators can still fall into error or delusion.
C) Because shudhūdh and ʿillah have nothing to do with the narrator.
D) Because the definition was made by later scholars.

Key Takeaway
Error and delusion are inevitable, even among reliable narrators, but their occurrence is rare and should be assessed case by case.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
beginner
6 min
Error and Forgetfulness as a Cause of Ikhtilaf
Explaining how error and forgetfulness lead to ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why error and forgetfulness are inevitable in hadith transmission and how they contribute to ikhtilaf among scholars.

Core Idea
Error and forgetfulness are inherent in human transmission, affecting even the most reliable narrators, and are a primary source of hadith disagreement.

This lesson explores a foundational concept in usul al-hadith: the inevitability of error (wahm) and forgetfulness (khata) even among trustworthy narrators. You will see how this reality leads to differences (ikhtilaf) between hadiths and why scholars have always acknowledged this. The passage by a classical author sets the stage by listing prerequisites for knowledge and then focusing on the first cause of ikhtilaf: error in narration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six prerequisites for knowledge
The author opens with a poem listing six conditions: intelligence, eagerness, diligence, proficiency, companionship of a teacher, and length of time. Eagerness (hirs) is emphasized as fundamental for hadith preservation.
2
Understand the role of eagerness in preservation
Even a narrator with weak memory must constantly review and safeguard his narrations to protect the Sunnah from error. This shows the effort required to minimize mistakes.
3
Recognize that error occurs even in trustworthy narrators
The passage asserts that error and forgetfulness happen even in the hadiths of thiqat (trustworthy narrators), which is why the definition of sahih requires absence of shudhudh (anomaly) and 'illa (defect), both stemming from error.
4
See how error leads to ikhtilaf
When a narrator makes an error, his narration may contradict other, more reliable narrations, causing ikhtilaf. The passage cites Yahya ibn Ma'in, Ahmad ibn Hanbal, Muslim, and al-Tirmidhi to confirm that no human is free from error.
Error and forgetfulness are listed as the first of the causes of ikhtilaf.
5
Note the testimonies from major hadith scholars
Each quoted scholar (Ahmad, Muslim, Tirmidhi) acknowledges that even the greatest preservers can err. This underscores that error is a universal human trait and a key source of disagreement.

الفصل التمهيدي بيان ماهية الاختلاف
أخي لن تنال العلم إلا بستة سأنبيك عن تفصيلها ببيان ذكاء وحرص واجتهاد وبلغة وصحبة أستاذ وطول زمان فالحرص إذن من أساسيات العلم، وإن قل حفظ الراوي أو كلت ذاكرته، فإن سعه الحفاظ على مروياته بالمذاكرة والمتابعة والتعاهد لمحفوظه ومراجعة أصوله، حفظاً للسنة النبوية من الخطأ فيها - بزيادة أو نقص أو تغيير -.
ومع هذا كله فإننا لم نعدم في تاريخنا الحديثي بعض الرواة الذين لم يبالوا بمروياتهم، ولم يولوها الاهتمام الكافي، سواء أهمل الراوي نفسه تعاهد محفوظاته أو مراجعته كتابه، أو تدخل عنصر بالعبث بمروياته، أو غير ذلك مما تكون نتيجته وقوع الوهم في حديث ذلك الراوي، ويؤول بالنهاية إلى حدوث الاختلاف مع روايات غيره، على أن الخطأ والوهم لم يسلم منه كبار الحفاظ شدة حرصهم وتوقيهم، لذا قال يحيى بن معين: لست أعجب ممن يحدث فيخطئ، إنما أعجب ممن يحدث فيصيب). غير أن الأحاديث التي حصل فيها الوهم تعد قليلة مغمورة في بحر ما رووه على الصواب.
وبإمكاننا أن فصل أسباب الاختلاف بما يأتي:
أولاً. الوهم والخطأ:
الخطأ والوهم أمران حاصلان وواقعان في أحاديث الثقات فضلاً عن وقوعه في أحاديث الضعفاء، ونحن وإن نذكر في حد الصحيح كون راويه تام الضبط إلا أن ذلك أمر نسبي)، وإلا فكيف اشترطنا في الصحيح أن لا يكون شاذاً ولا معللاً مع كون راويه ثقة فيتخرج على هذا أن الوهم والخطأ يدخل في أحاديث الثقات؛ لأن كلا من الشذوذ والعلة داخل بمعنى الوهم والخطأ. ثم إن الوهم والخطأ من الأسباب الرئيسة للاختلاف بين الأحاديث. وبالسبر والنظر إلى كتب السنة النبوية نجد عدداً كبيراً من الرواة الثقات قد أخطأوا في بعض ما رووا، وهو أمر متفاوت بين الرواة حسب مروياتهم قلة وكثرة وربما كان حظ من أكثر من الرواية أكبر حظاً من المقلين؛ لذا نجد غلطات عدت على الأئمة العلماء الحفاظ لكنها لم تؤثر عليهم في سعة ما رووه، قال الإمام أحمد بن حنبل: (ومن يعرى من الخطأ والتصحيف). وقال الإمام مسلم بن الحجاج: فليس من ناقل خبر وحامل أثر من السلف الماضين إلى زماننا - وإن كان أحفظ الناس وأشدهم توقياً وإتقاناً لما يحفظ وينقل - إلا الغلط والسهو ممكن في حفظه ونقله.

The preliminary chapter: Explanation of the nature of difference. O brother, you will not attain knowledge except through six: I will inform you of their detail with an explanation: intelligence, eagerness, diligence, proficiency, companionship of a teacher, and length of time. So eagerness is among the fundamentals of knowledge. Even if the narrator's memorization is little or his memory is weak, his capacity for preserving his narrations through review, follow-up, revisiting his memorization, and consulting his sources - to preserve the Prophetic Sunnah from error in it - by addition, omission, or alteration - is [important]. And with all this, we have not lacked in our hadith history some narrators who did not care about their narrations, and did not give them sufficient attention, whether the narrator himself neglected to review his memorizations or consult his book, or an element intervened to tamper with his narrations, or other things resulting in the occurrence of error (wahm) in that narrator's hadith, ultimately leading to difference with others' narrations. However, error and forgetfulness did not spare even the major preservers despite their intense care and caution. Hence Yahya ibn Ma'in said: 'I do not marvel at one who narrates and errs; I only marvel at one who narrates and hits the mark.' Nonetheless, the hadiths in which error occurred are few, submerged in the sea of what they narrated correctly. We can detail the causes of difference as follows: Firstly: Error and Forgetfulness: Error and forgetfulness are things that occur and happen in the hadiths of trustworthy narrators, let alone in the hadiths of weak narrators. Even though we mention in the definition of sound (sahih) that its narrator is complete in precision (dabt), that is relative; otherwise, how have we stipulated in the sound [hadith] that it be neither anomalous (shadhdh) nor defective (mu'allal) while its narrator is trustworthy? Thus it follows that error and forgetfulness enter into the hadiths of trustworthy narrators, because both anomaly and defect are included in the meaning of error and forgetfulness. Then indeed error and forgetfulness are among the main causes of difference between hadiths. By investigation and examination of the books of the Prophetic Sunnah, we find a large number of trustworthy narrators who made mistakes in some of what they narrated, and it varies among narrators according to their narrations, so perhaps the share of one who narrates more is greater than the share of those who narrate less. Hence we find mistakes attributed to the imams, scholars, preservers, but they did not affect them given the vastness of what they narrated. Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal said: 'Who is free from error and tashif?' Imam Muslim ibn al-Hajjaj said: 'There is no transmitter of reports or carrier of traditions from the past predecessors to our time - even if he is the most retentive of people and the most cautious and meticulous in what he memorizes and transmits - except that error and forgetfulness are possible in his memorization and transmission.' Imam al-Tirmidhi said: 'No one of the imams was spared from error and mistake despite their memorization.' Then al-Tirmidhi cited numerous narrations indicating the variation of scholars in memory and their differential in precision and infrequency of error. Then he said: 'The discussion on this and the narrations from the scholars are many, and we have only presented some of it briefly so that it may serve as a guide to the ranks of scholars and their differential in memory and perfection, and [to know] why any scholar criticized another.' Since error in narration is a self-evident matter, and no human is free from it, we find the great ones have produced...
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage is from the preliminary chapter explaining the nature of ikhtilaf (difference) in hadith. The author opens with a famous poem listing six prerequisites for attaining knowledge: intelligence, eagerness, diligence, proficiency, a teacher's companionship, and lengthy study. Eagerness (hirs) is emphasized as fundamental, especially for hadith preservation: a narrator, even with weak memory, must constantly review and safeguard his narrations to protect the Sunnah from error. The author then notes that despite this, some narrators were negligent, leading to error (wahm) and ultimately to ikhtilaf with other narrations. However, even major preservers (huffaz) were not immune to error, as Yahya ibn Ma'in observed: it is more remarkable to narrate correctly than to err. The passage then lists the first cause of ikhtilaf: error and forgetfulness (al-wahm wa al-khata). It asserts that these occur even in the hadith of trustworthy narrators, which is why the definition of sahih requires absence of shudhudh (anomaly) and 'illa (defect), both of which stem from error. The author supports this with citations from Ahmad ibn Hanbal, Muslim, and al-Tirmidhi, all confirming that no scholar is free from error, and that mistakes are more common among those who narrate extensively. Thus error is a major cause of ikhtilaf between hadiths.

Key Terms
الوهم (al-wahm): Error or illusion in hadith narration that leads to mistake.
الخطأ (al-khata): Mistake or error in hadith transmission.
الشذوذ (al-shudhudh): Anomaly in hadith when a trustworthy narrator contradicts a more reliable one.
العلة (al-'illa): Hidden defect that impairs the soundness of a hadith.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because they intentionally change the text.
B) Because error and forgetfulness are possible for all humans, even the most careful.
C) Because they rely on weak sources.
D) Because they do not review their books.

Key Takeaway
Error and forgetfulness are unavoidable in hadith transmission and are a primary cause of ikhtilaf, even among the most reliable narrators.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate

Definition and Impact of Ikhtilat in Hadith
Defining ikhtilat and its effect on narration and juristic differences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define ikhtilat, identify its causes, and explain its legal impact on the reliability of narrations in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
Ikhtilat is a mental affliction that renders a narrator's hadith unreliable unless pre-ikhtilat narrations are identified or corroborated.

Differences among jurists often trace back to variations in hadith narrations. One key source of such variation is 'ikhtilat' – a mental confusion that afflicts narrators due to old age or trauma. This lesson unpacks the definition and causes of ikhtilat, and shows how it affects the acceptability of hadith as evidence, a critical step in the Hanafi process of deriving rulings.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the Linguistic and Technical Definition
Start by reading the linguistic root: 'khalata' means to mix. Technically, ikhtilat is a corruption of the mind causing disorder in speech and actions. Note the key phrase 'fasad al-'aql wa 'adam intizam al-aqwal wa al-af'al'.
The definition is from al-Sakhawi, a major hadith scholar.
2
Identify the Causes of Ikhtilat
The passage lists causes: senility (old age), harm, illness, death of a son, theft of money, loss of books, or burning of books. These incidents trigger confusion that affects narration.
Causes are not exhaustive; any event impairing mental faculties qualifies.
3
Understand the Effect on Narrator Reliability
Once ikhtilat sets in, the narrator's subsequent narrations become weak (da'if). They cannot oppose authentic (sahih) narrations from trustworthy narrators. This is because a weak narration does not invalidate a sound one.
The Hanafi principle: 'al-riwayah al-sahihah la tu'allu bi al-riwayah al-da'ifah'.
4
Learn When a Mukhtaliṭ's Narration is Accepted
Two exceptions: (1) if the narrator's narration is from before the onset of ikhtilat, identified as 'ma haddatha bihi qabla al-ikhtilat'; (2) if the weak narration is corroborated (mutaba'ah) by another reliable chain.
This distinction is crucial for hadith criticism and later for weighing evidential value.
5
Connect to Juristic Differences
Because different schools may weigh narrations differently, a hadith that is rejected due to ikhtilat in one school may be accepted in another if the narrators' conditions are assessed differently. This leads to variant rulings.
Hanafi usul emphasizes careful scrutiny of narrators' states.

فأخذ عَنْهُ عشرين حديثاً، فلقيه صاحبٌ لَهُ وَهُوَ راجع، فسأله رؤيتها، وَكَانَ ثمة ريح شديدة، فذهبت بالأوراق من يد الرجل، فصار هشيم يحدّث بِمَا علق مِنْهَا بذهنه، وَلَمْ يَكُنْ أتقن حفظها، فوهم في ، ثُمَّ حدث من حفظه فدخل الوهم والاختلاف في حديثه ). ثالثاً. الاختلاط الاختلاط لغة: يقال خلطت الشيء بغيره خَلْطاً فاختلط، وخالطه مخالطة وخلاطاً، واختلط فلان، أي: فسد عقله، والتخليط في الأمر: الإفساد فيه والمختلط من الاختلاط، واختلط عقله إذا تغير فهو مختلط، واختلط عقله (فسد) أما في اصطلاح المحدثين : فَقَدْ قَالَ السخاوي): «وحقيقته فساد العقل وعدم انتظام الأقوال والأفعال، إما بخرف، أو ضرر، أو مرض أو عرض من موت ابن وسرقة مال كالمسعودي (٢) ، أو ذهاب كتب كابن لهيعة (۳)، أو احتراقها كابن الملقن (٤)) . إذن الاختلاط: آفة عقلية تورث فساداً في الإدراك، وتصيب الإنسان في آخر عمره، أو تعرض له بسبب حادث لفقد عزيز أو ضياع مال؛ ومن تصبه هذه الآفة لكبر سِنّهِ يقال فِيْهِ: اختلط بأخرة، ويقال: بآخره (۳ ) . فالاختلاط قَدْ يطرأ عَلَى كثير من رواة الْحَدِيث النبوي مِمَّا يؤثر عَلَى روايته أحياناً فيدخل في رِوَايَته الوهم والخطأ مِمَّا يؤدي ذَلِكَ بالمحصلة النهائية إلى وجود الاختلاف بَيْنَ الروايات ثُمَّ من كَانَ مختلطاً فدخل الوهم في حديثه لا تضر روايته رِوَايَةَ الثقات الأثبات؛ إِذْ إِنَّ الرِّوَايَة الصَّحِيحَة لا تُعلُّ بالرواية الضعيفة، فرواية المختلط ضعيفة لا تقاوم رِوَايَة الثقات، ولا تصلح للحجية إلا إذا توبع المختلط في روايته أو كَانَتْ روايته مِمَّا حدث بِهِ قَبْلَ الاختلاط وعلماؤنا الأجلاء أحرقوا أعمارهم شموعاً تضيء لنا الطريق من أجل بَيَان كُلّ ما يدخل الْحَدِيث من خطأ ووهم واختلاف، إذ إنّ مَعْرِفَة المختلطين لَيْسَ بالأمر السهل بَلْ هُوَ أمرٌ شاقٌ عَلَى الْمُحَدِّثِينَ للغاية، بَلْ كَانَ
He took from him twenty hadiths, then a companion of his met him while he was returning, and asked to see them. There was a strong wind, which blew the papers from the man's hand, so Hushaym began narrating from what stuck in his mind, and he had not perfected memorizing them, so he made mistakes in some of them, thus his hadith was weakened because of that, especially concerning al-Zuhri. This was an incidental matter affecting Hushaym, who is a trustworthy one among the great, noble trustworthy narrators; his hadith is included by the authors of the six books, but he was weakened specifically concerning al-Zuhri due to this incident that happened to him, so that al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar said: 'As for his narration from al-Zuhri, there is none of it in the two Sahihs.' Likewise, the condition of a narrator's precision varies according to circumstances, places, and shaykhs, due to the lack of means enabling him to preserve what he heard from some of his shaykhs, or because of the loss of some of what he wrote from some of his shaykhs, even if he is among the most reliable people concerning that particular shaykh. Among the incidental circumstances mentioned is what happened to Mu'ammal ibn Isma'il, when he had buried his books, then narrated from memory, so error and difference entered his hadith. Third: al-Ikhtilat. Al-Ikhtilat linguistically: it is said 'khalata al-shay'a bi-ghayrihi khalṭan fa-ikhtalaṭa', and 'khalatahu mukhalatan wa khilāṭan', and 'ikhtalaṭa fulān', meaning his mind became corrupted, and 'al-takhlīṭ fī al-amr' means spoiling it. 'al-mukhtaliṭ' is from 'al-ikhtilāṭ', and 'ikhtalaṭa 'aqluhu' means it changed, so he is 'mukhtaliṭ', and 'ikhtalaṭa 'aqluhu' (became corrupted). As for the terminology of hadith scholars: al-Sakhawi said: 'Its reality is corruption of the mind and lack of order in speech and actions, either due to senility, harm, illness, or an occurrence such as the death of a son or theft of money, like al-Mas'udi, or loss of books like Ibn Lahi'a, or their burning like Ibn al-Mulaqqin.' Thus, al-ikhtilat is a mental affliction that causes corruption in perception, and affects a person in the latter part of his life, or occurs due to an incident of losing a dear one or loss of wealth. One who is afflicted by this due to old age is said: 'ikhtalaṭa bi-ākhirih' and 'bi-ākhirih'. So ikhtilat may occur to many narrators of prophetic hadith, affecting their narration at times, causing error and mistake to enter their narrations, ultimately leading to differences between narrations. Then, for one who is mukhtaliṭ and error entered his hadith, his narration does not harm the narration of trustworthy, reliable narrators; for a sound narration is not invalidated by a weak narration. The narration of a mukhtaliṭ is weak and does not oppose the narration of trustworthy narrators, nor is it valid as evidence unless the mukhtaliṭ is followed in his narration or his narration is from what he narrated before the ikhtilat. Our venerable scholars have burned their lives as candles illuminating the path for us, in order to explain everything that enters hadith of error, mistake, and difference. Indeed, knowing the mukhtaliṭūn is not an easy matter; rather it is extremely difficult for hadith scholars, rather it was...
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage is part of a preliminary chapter explaining the nature of differences among jurists. The author discusses various causes for differences in hadith narrations, which in turn lead to juristic differences. Here, he focuses on the first two causes: incidental circumstances (like the wind blowing away Hushaym's papers) and the loss of written notes. Then he delves into the third cause: 'ikhtilat' (confusion/mental affliction). He defines ikhtilat linguistically and technically, explaining that it is a mental deterioration affecting elderly narrators or those who suffer a traumatic event. This condition introduces errors into their narrations. Importantly, the passage clarifies that such weak narrations do not override authentic ones, and they can only be accepted as evidence if the narrator's pre-ikhtilat narrations are distinguished or if he is corroborated. This demonstrates the meticulous approach of hadith scholars in preserving the integrity of the prophetic tradition and highlights a key source of variation in fiqh rulings.

Key Terms
الاختلاط (al-ikhtilāṭ): A mental affliction that causes corruption of the mind and lack of order in speech and actions, leading to errors in hadith narration.
المختلط (al-mukhtaliṭ): A narrator who has become confused due to old age or trauma, leading to unreliable narrations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) If the narrator is generally known to be trustworthy

C) If the narration does not contradict the Quran
D) If the narrator repents after the incident

Key Takeaway
Ikhtilat weakens a narrator's later transmissions, which are accepted only if pre-ikhtilat or corroborated—a critical factor in Hanafi usul for assessing hadith evidence and explaining juristic differences.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement

Three Categories of Mixed Narrators (Mukhtalitin) – A Hanafi Usul Analysis
Classification of narrators based on ikhtilat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify a narrator based on his ikhtilat and determine whether his hadith are acceptable as evidence in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Not all confused narrators are equally weak; the key is whether they narrated before or after the confusion.

In hadith criticism, some narrators suffered from memory deterioration (ikhtilat) in later life. Al-'Ala'i presents a three-part classification that helps us assess the impact of such confusion. This lesson unpacks that classification and shows how Hanafi usul applies it to determine whether a narrator's hadith can be used as proof for legal rulings.

Guided Path
1
Recall the definition of ikhtilat
Ikhtilat is a narrator's mental confusion or memory loss in old age. It affects the reliability of his hadith.
Not all narrators with ikhtilat are automatically rejected.
2
Identify the three categories from the passage
Read the passage carefully. The first category includes narrators whose confusion did not weaken them (due to brevity or because they did not narrate during it). The second includes those already weak before confusion. The third includes originally reliable narrators who later became confused.
Each category has different implications for acceptance.
3
Apply the Hanafi usul principle to each category
For the first category, the narrator remains trustworthy (thiqah). For the second, his weakness increases. For the third, his hadith are only accepted if we can distinguish what he narrated before the confusion.
In Hanafi usul, the default is to accept hadith from a trustworthy narrator unless there is clear evidence of unreliability.
4
Determine the practical ruling for each
First category: hadith accepted absolutely. Second: hadith rejected or considered very weak. Third: need to check the chain – if the narrator's narrations are clearly from before the confusion, they are accepted; otherwise, they are problematic.
This classification helps the jurist decide whether to use a hadith as evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال العلائي: «أما الرواة الذين حصل لهم الاختلاط في آخر عمرهم فهم على ثلاثة أقسام: أحدها: من لم يوجب ذلك له ضعفاً أصلاً، ولم يحط من مرتبته؛ إما لقصر مدة الاختلاط وقلته كسفيان بن عيينة، وإسحاق بن إبراهيم بن راهويه، وهما من أئمة الإسلام المتفق عليهم؛ وإما لأنه لم يرو شيئاً حال اختلاطه، فسلم حديثه من الوهم كجرير بن حازم وعفان بن مسلم، ونحوهما. ثانيها: من كان متكلماً فيه قبل الاختلاط، فلم يحصل من الاختلاط إلا زيادة في ضعفه؛ كابن لهيعة، ومحمد بن جابر السحيمي، ونحوهما. ثالثها: من كان محتجاً به، ثم اختلط، أو عمر في آخر عمره، فحصل الاضطراب فيما روى بعد ذلك، فيتوقف الاحتجاج به على التمييز بين ما حدث به قبل الاختلاط عما رواه بعد ذلك».
Al-'Ala'i said: "As for the narrators who suffered from confusion (ikhtilat) in their later life, they fall into three categories: First: those for whom this did not cause any weakness at all and did not lower their rank; either due to the brevity and scarcity of the confusion, like Sufyan ibn 'Uyaynah and Ishaq ibn Ibrahim ibn Rahawayh—both are unanimously accepted imams of Islam—or because they did not narrate anything during their confusion, so their hadith remained free from error, like Jarir ibn Hazim and 'Affan ibn Muslim, and similar ones. Second: those who were already criticized before the confusion, so the confusion only increased their weakness, like Ibn Lahi'ah and Muhammad ibn Jabir al-Sahimi, and similar ones. Third: those who were relied upon (as proof), then became confused, or lived long into old age, so confusion occurred in what they narrated thereafter; thus relying on them depends on distinguishing between what they narrated before the confusion and what they narrated after it."
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage is a classification of narrators who suffered from ikhtilat (confusion or memory deterioration) in their later years, as quoted from the hadith scholar al-'Ala'i. The author provides three categories: First, narrators whose confusion was so brief or minimal that it did not affect their reliability, such as Sufyan ibn 'Uyaynah and Ishaq ibn Rahawayh, or those who stopped narrating after the confusion (like Jarir ibn Hazim). Second, narrators who were already weak before confusion, so it only exacerbated their weakness, like Ibn Lahi'ah. Third, narrators who were originally trustworthy but then became confused in old age, making their later narrations unreliable unless clearly distinguished from earlier ones. In Hanafi usul, such classifications affect the acceptance of hadith as evidence for rulings, since ahadith from confused narrators are only accepted if transmitted before the confusion or if the chain is clear.

Key Terms
اختلاط (ikhtilat): Confusion or memory deterioration in a narrator's later life, affecting the reliability of his hadith.
مختلط (mukhtalit): A narrator who experienced ikhtilat; his hadith are accepted only if transmitted before the confusion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which category of mixed narrators includes narrators like Ibn Lahi'ah?
A) Those whose confusion did not weaken them at all.
B) Those who were already weak before confusion.
C) Those who were reliable but became confused in old age.
D) Those who never narrated after confusion.

Key Takeaway
The acceptance of a mukhtalit narrator's hadith depends on his category: brief/no narration during confusion (accepted), pre-existing weakness (rejected), or need to distinguish pre-/post-confusion narrations.

Loss of Eyesight and Its Impact on Hadith Precision
Explains how loss of eyesight affects narrator precision and leads to differing narrations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how loss of eyesight can affect a narrator's dabt and how this contributes to differences in hadith narrations, applying Hanafi usul criteria.

Core Idea
Loss of eyesight can impair a narrator's dabt, leading to errors that cause variation in hadith and consequently in fiqh rulings.

This lesson explores the fourth cause of hadith variation: narrator blindness. We will define dabt (precision) as a cornerstone of hadith acceptance, distinguish its types, and examine how the loss of eyesight can erode dabt. Using examples from the source, we will see how Hanafi usul evaluates such cases and why this is a source of legitimate ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
Define dabt and its types
Start by understanding dabt as a condition for hadith authenticity. Identify its two types: apparent (linguistic) and inner (meaning/jurisprudence). Recognize that absolute dabt is condition for narrator reliability.
The text clarifies that apparent dabt suffices because transmission by meaning is permissible.
2
Identify the role of eyesight in maintaining dabt
Eyesight is crucial for reviewing written records (kitab) and refreshing memory (sadr). Loss of sight can hinder a narrator's ability to maintain accuracy, particularly if they relied on books.
Some narrators use assistants; others depend entirely on memory.
3
Analyze how loss of eyesight leads to errors
When a narrator loses eyesight, his precision may decline, allowing errors (wahm) to enter. Scholars compare his narrations to those of reliable peers; frequent disagreement indicates impaired dabt.
Not all blind narrators become unreliable; each case is assessed individually.
4
Apply the principle to examples and ikhtilaf
Study the examples of Abd al-Razzaq and Ali ibn Mus-hir. Consider how their blindness affected their narrations and could cause fiqh differences when their hadith are weighed against others.
Hanafi usul requires careful evaluation; such differences can lead to legitimate ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رابعاً. ذهاب البصر :
من المعروف في بدائه علم الحديث أنّ الضبط شرط أساسي في صحة الحديث النبوي الشريف، والضبط: هو إتقان ما يرويه الراوي بأن يكون متيقظاً لما يروي غير مغفل، حافظاً لروايته إن روى من حفظه ضابطاً لكتابه إن روى من الكتاب عالماً بمعنى ما يرويه، وبما يحيل المعنى عن المراد إن روى بالمعنى، حتى يثق المطلع على روايته والمتتبع لأحواله بأنه أدى الأمانة كما تحملها، لم يغير منها شيئاً، وهذا مناط التفاضل بين الرواة الثقات، فإذا كان الراوي عدلاً ضابطاً سمي ثقة. ويعرف ضبطه بموافقة الثقات الضابطين المتقنين إذا اعتبر حديثه بحديثهم، ولا تضر مخالفته النادرة لهم، فإن كثرت مخالفته لهم، وندرت الموافقة، اختل ضبطه ولم يحتج بحديثه.
والضبط نوعان: ظاهر وباطن.
فالظاهر من حيث اللغة. والباطن: ضبط معناه من حيث تعلق الحكم الشرعي به، وهو الفقه ومطلق الضبط الذي هو شرط الراوي، هو الضبط ظاهراً عند الأكثر؛ لأنه يجوز نقل الحديث بالمعنى عند الكثير من العلماء.
فمما تقدم نستخلص أن الضبط قسمان ضبط صدر، وضبط كتاب وضابط الكتاب يحتاج أن يقرأ كتابه من أجل الرواية والمقابلة، وضابط الصدر يحتاج إلى أن يعاود حفظه وكتابه من أجل ضبط مروياته، وربما يمكن أن يحصل هذا لبعض الرواة بمفردهم، وقسم منهم يستعين بمن يثق به ليعاونه على ذلك. إذن فالبصر مهم في ذلك وله دور كبير في المحافظة على الحفظ؛ لذا فإنّ زوال البصر وذهابه قد يؤدي بالمحصلة النهائية إلى دخول الوهم في بعض روايات المحدثين مما يؤدي إلى حصول اختلاف بين الروايات.
ومن الذين ذهب بصرهم: عبد الرزاق بن همام الصنعاني صاحب المصنف قال الحافظ ابن حجر العسقلاني: عمي في آخر عمره فتغير. وكذا علي بن مسهر قال العجلي: صاحب سنة ثقة في الحديث صالح الكتاب كثير الرواية عن الكوفيين، وقال أبو عبد الله أحمد بن حنبل لما سئل عنه: لا أدري كيف أقول كان قد ذهب بصره فكان يحدثهم من حفظه.
Fourth: Loss of eyesight. It is known in the rudiments of hadith science that precision is an essential condition for the authenticity of the noble prophetic hadith. Precision is: mastery of what the narrator narrates, such that he is attentive to what he narrates, not heedless; he is a memorizer of his narration if he narrates from memory, a keeper of his book if he narrates from a book, knowledgeable of the meaning of what he narrates, and of what changes the meaning from what is intended if he narrates by meaning, so that the one who examines his narration and follows his circumstances is confident that he fulfilled the trust as he received it, not changing anything from it. This is the criterion of differentiation among trustworthy narrators. If the narrator is upright and precise, he is called trustworthy. His precision is known by agreement with precise, trustworthy, and masterful narrators when his hadith is compared to theirs. His rare disagreement does not harm, but if his disagreement becomes frequent and agreement rare, his precision becomes impaired and his hadith is not used as evidence. Precision is of two types: apparent and inner. The apparent is from the perspective of language. The inner is the precision of its meaning in terms of the attachment of legal rulings to it; it is jurisprudence. The absolute precision that is a condition for the narrator is apparent precision according to the majority, because transmission of hadith by meaning is permissible according to many scholars. From the foregoing, we conclude that precision is of two types: chest precision and book precision. The keeper of a book needs to read his book for narration and comparison; the keeper of the chest needs to review his memory and his book to maintain his narrations. Some narrators may accomplish this alone, while others seek help from someone they trust to assist them. Thus, eyesight is important in this and has a great role in preserving memory. Therefore, loss of eyesight may ultimately lead to the entry of error in some narrations of hadith scholars, leading to differences among narrations. Among those who lost their eyesight: Abd al-Razzaq ibn Hammam al-San'ani, author of al-Musannaf; al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar al-Asqalani said: 'He became blind at the end of his life and changed.' Similarly, Ali ibn Mus-hir; al-Ajli said: 'He was a man of sunnah, trustworthy in hadith, his book was sound, he narrated many from the Kufans.' Abu Abd Allah Ahmad ibn Hanbal, when asked about him, said: 'I do not know what to say; he had lost his eyesight and would narrate to them from memory.'
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage discusses the fourth cause of variation in hadith: the loss of eyesight by a narrator. It begins by defining precision (dabt), which is a fundamental condition for hadith authenticity. The author explains that precision is of two types: apparent (related to language) and inner (related to understanding the meaning and legal implications). The majority of scholars consider apparent precision sufficient because transmission by meaning is widely permitted. The passage then elaborates on two subcategories: precision of the chest (memory) and precision of the book (written records). Since eyesight is crucial for reviewing written records and maintaining memory, its loss can lead to errors and consequently to differences among hadith texts. Examples of narrators who lost their eyesight are given: Abd al-Razzaq al-San'ani, who became blind and changed, and Ali ibn Mus-hir, who narrated from memory after losing his sight. The Hanafi school, like other schools, relies on precise narrators; such loss of precision affects the acceptance of hadith and thus can lead to fiqh differences.

Key Terms
الضبط (al-dabt): Precision in narration, including both memory accuracy and written record keeping
ذهاب البصر (dhahab al-basar): Loss of eyesight, which can impair a narrator's ability to maintain precision

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary reason that loss of eyesight can lead to differences in hadith?
A) The narrator can no longer verify his written records, leading to memory errors.
B) The narrator becomes blind and thus stops narrating altogether.
C) The narrator loses his ability to understand the meaning of hadith.
D) The narrator becomes untrustworthy due to sin.

Key Takeaway
Loss of eyesight can impair dabt, leading to errors in hadith and contributing to fiqh differences; scholars evaluate each narrator individually.
